German Government Announces Retrieval of Internal River Navigation Rights, Final Restrictions of the Peace Treaty Abolished 56

(Berlin) The German government, at 1:00 PM today, notified the fourteen nations of Britain, France, Italy, Belgium, Austria, Czechoslovakia, Poland, Denmark, Sweden, Lithuania, Romania, Yugoslavia, the Netherlands, and Hungary, that it was abolishing Chapter Twelve of Part II of the Treaty of Versailles, which concerned regulations for navigation on rivers within Germany. According to these regulations, the Elbe, Oder, and other rivers within Germany, as well as the Rhine, Danube, and Niemen, which border other countries, were to be considered international rivers. Vessels of all nations would be free to navigate these rivers, and an international commission would be established to oversee the implementation of this navigation system. The German government's action clearly indicates that it no longer recognizes this commission. According to official sources here, the government's action is purely politically motivated, with the aim of restoring the country's rightful sovereignty over its rivers. However, the navigation systems of certain rivers, such as the Elbe and Rhine, will not be changed. As for the ports of Hamburg and Stettin, which have traditionally been free ports available for the free use of Czechoslovakia, this will continue unchanged. (Havas, 14th)

(London) After receiving this notification, political figures in Britain predict that the government will likely engage in negotiations with the German government soon. They believe that this action by Germany will inevitably have a significant impact on the trade issues of many countries involved. Political figures generally do not approve of Germany's actions but are not surprised, as Germany has been preparing for weeks to remove the last restrictions imposed on it by the Treaty of Versailles, so this action was expected. (Havas, 14th)

(Paris) Here, there is no excessive surprise at Hitler's recent actions. Although it is recognized that Hitler's move is no different in principle from Germany's disregard for other clauses of the Treaty of Versailles, in practice, it will not lead to any changes. It is said that France has no practical way to utilize the navigation rights permitted in the treaty. Hitler's move may affect Czech shipping on the Elbe to Hamburg and the North Sea, the barge industry along the Rhine River in the Netherlands, and other international routes. All of these shipping industries will likely suffer a significant blow, as they will now be subject to any regulations imposed by Germany. (Reuters, 14th)

Covenant Issue, Belgian Proposal, Advocating Detailed Explanation of All Articles 57

(Geneva) The Secretariat of the League of Nations, following the resolution of the League Assembly in July of this year, requested opinions from member states regarding amendments to the Covenant. Responses have been received from various governments one after another, and the Belgian government's reply was also received recently and made public today by the Secretariat of the League of Nations. The Belgian reply proposes that certain articles of the Covenant, especially Article 16, should be explained in detail. For example, the scope of the obligations and assistance that member states can and should bear to a country that has been invaded must be clearly defined. In addition, the Belgian reply requests that amendments to the Covenant should be adopted using the method used in 1921, preferring to retain the original articles and adopt additional articles separately, rather than revising the entire Covenant. Finally, the Belgian reply urges all countries to join the League of Nations. (Havas, 14th)

This base will cover 1,200 square feet and will be surrounded by breakwaters, with a canal dug as an entrance to the port. The annual recurring cost will be approximately $15,000. This base was originally intended for the development of commercial aviation, but military authorities have openly stated that it will be of great use to U.S. national defense. (Tokyo) According to a telegram from Washington, the United States believes that the Pacific defense restriction treaty should be terminated and has decided to build a powerful air base on Midway Island. Although this development was anticipated, Midway Island is located in the center of the Pacific and is a strategically important base. Therefore, the Japanese Navy attaches great importance to it. The United States is still adhering to its plan for transoceanic operations. Building a base on Midway Island, which is further west than Hawaii, can be said to be moving its base approximately 800 miles further west. Thus, with Midway Island to the east, the Aleutian Islands to the north, and Luzon Island in the Philippines to the south, the United States is consolidating its encirclement of Japan. The advancement of the U.S. Air Force to Midway Island will shorten the distance to Tokyo to within 2,000 miles. The threat posed by the U.S. Air Force's giant seaplanes stationed there is significant, so the Japanese military authorities are extremely concerned about this development and believe it is necessary to devise comprehensive countermeasures. (Domei News Agency, 14th)

British-Italian Talks, Preliminary Exchange of Views on Mediterranean Issues 63

(London) Foreign Secretary Eden met last night with Italian Ambassador to Britain Grandi to discuss relations between Britain and Italy for a considerable period of time. It is reported that Eden indicated to Grandi that the British government is prepared to accept the Anglo-Italian Gentleman's Agreement proposed by Italian Prime Minister Mussolini and is willing to begin negotiations with the Italian government to conclude this agreement in the shortest possible time. Britain also proposes to divide the Mediterranean into several different spheres of influence. These spheres of influence can be defined by declarations issued separately by the governments concerned. Once the spheres of influence have been demarcated, the governments concerned should promise to respect each other's interests. Before the commencement of formal negotiations on the above proposals, preliminary negotiations should be held between Britain and Italy. The purpose of these preliminary negotiations is to resolve all outstanding issues between the two countries, namely: (1) the Mediterranean shipping route issue; (2) the issue of mutual spheres of influence of Britain and Italy in countries outside Europe; (3) the Suez Canal issue; and (4) the naval balance of power issue. Only after these issues have been resolved can formal negotiations between Britain and Italy begin on this basis. (Havas, 14th)

Thirty Aircraft Engage in Combat 6,000 Feet Above Madrid, Champion Aircraft Wins with High Speed, Many Rebel Aircraft Shot Down 65

Madrid. This agency's special correspondent reports that at around 11:00 AM today, a total of thirty aircraft belonging to the government forces and the Nationalist forces engaged in a dogfight over the city. After twenty minutes, three of them crashed. One of them was on fire, resembling a giant torch falling from the sky. The crew members were burned to death on the spot. As for the other two that crashed, the pilots parachuted down. This agency's reporter could not determine which side the three aircraft belonged to. The other aircraft continued to fight. The fighting ceased somewhat at around 3:00 PM. The sound of machine guns was incessant. In addition, there were five major fires in Madrid today. According to investigations by reporters, the Las Islas railway station, a cigarette factory, and the contagious disease school were all on fire. (Havas, 14th)

Madrid. Five rebel three-engine bombers and nine fighter planes flew over Madrid this afternoon and engaged in fierce combat with sixteen government aircraft at an altitude of 6,000 feet for thirty minutes. Residents of the capital all looked up to watch. Soon, one rebel aircraft was seen crashing to the ground, and the pilot was killed on the spot. One government aircraft crashed soon after. The pilot had a parachute and was spared from danger, but he was unconscious after landing. Several people came forward a few minutes later to release him from the parachute. Several other aircraft disappeared during the fierce battle. As of tonight, there is no news. Ten government aircraft patrolled the sky after the battle, and enemy aircraft dared not approach. (National Telegram, 13th)

Madrid. Government and rebel aircraft engaged in two fierce battles in the skies over here today. The result was that the government aircraft were victorious. The rebel aircraft, in addition to eight being shot down, were all repelled. The first battle took place at 8:00 AM. This agency's reporter, O'China, witnessed the event. At that time, ten rebel aircraft appeared in the sky. In order to avoid anti-aircraft guns, they flew very high. Residents of the capital, seeing the enemy aircraft approaching, rushed to underground rooms in various places. At 8:05 AM, fifteen government fighter planes appeared in the sky. The pilots of both sides were extremely skilled. The flight altitude was 2,000 meters at the highest and only 400 meters above the ground at the lowest. The fighting lasted a long time. Residents who had not had time to hide watched the battle in the open air, forgetting the danger. At first, both sides had their successes. Then, one enemy aircraft's wing was hit and shattered, causing it to crash. One pilot inside deployed a parachute and slowly descended. However, it was not known where he landed. Soon after, another rebel aircraft was shot down. At this time, the government aircraft regrouped, numbering fifteen. The crowd on the ground cheered loudly. The remaining eight rebel aircraft attempted to escape but were surrounded by government aircraft. One more was hit and crashed. The government aircraft finally pursued the rebels to the outskirts of Madrid and shot down three more enemy aircraft, bringing the total of rebel aircraft shot down to six. Only four escaped, while no government aircraft were lost. At 3:30 PM, three rebel large bombers appeared in the sky. At that time, the sky was clear and blue. Anti-aircraft guns immediately fired and bombarded the enemy aircraft. About fifteen minutes later, ten rebel light aircraft appeared in the sky. At that time, the ground audience eagerly awaited the government aircraft to respond. In less than a few minutes, ten government aircraft suddenly appeared and bravely pursued the enemy aircraft. The two sides fought fiercely for an hour. The government forces were victorious again. Two rebel aircraft were shot down, and the rest escaped. The people, seeing the government air force's combat skills so miraculous, were all exhilarated and greatly inspired. (Havas, 13th)

Madrid. Commander of Defense General Miaja was greatly excited about the results of yesterday's air battle and the victory of the counterattack. Today, he went to the front lines to express his condolences and encourage the soldiers to quickly eliminate the rebels. This morning, Miaja told the City Defense Committee that the defense of the capital can be maintained for a year. (National Telegram, 13th)

Improved Morale of the Spanish Militia, New Weapons Arriving Steadily, Mostly Italian-Made Rifles, An Englishwoman Describes Life in the Besieged City 68

Madrid – The morale of the militia has greatly improved recently. For about a week, they have been quite successful in resisting the Moorish and foreign troops, realizing that these enemies are not invincible. The steady arrival of new war materials from abroad is also a reason for boosting the morale of the defending forces. The garrison troops are now mostly equipped with Italian-made rifles. It's ironic that weapons manufactured by the Fascists are being used to kill Fascists. Madrid's strategic position is quite unique. The Nationalists' main attack comes from the Toledo-Andalusia road, which is difficult to traverse. The many houses, embankments, airfields, and camps along the way can all be used as small fortresses, resulting in much street fighting since the beginning of the war. This is why Nationalist planes frequently attack this area. An offensive from the Casa de Campo area would be easier because the dense forests provide cover, but it would require crossing a vast plain, which is dominated by government machine guns. (Reuters, 14th)

Madrid – An Englishwoman who has been living in the capital since the outbreak of the civil war described life in the besieged city to a Reuters correspondent today. She said that shopping is extremely difficult. This morning, a mile-long queue had formed outside a fish shop. Laundry is also a problem, because after washing, there is insufficient electricity to iron the clothes, so they remain damp and uncomfortable to wear. Gas supply has long been cut off. Fashionable clothing is a thing of the past, as women who dress fashionably are seen as middle class and are easily insulted. She has removed the fur collar from her coat. Traveling is dangerous because of frequent air raids. Many women are killed by bombs while gathering to shop. The woman also said that she is accustomed to air raids. Whenever she hears the sound of bombs exploding, she lies flat on the ground, as this is the only way to protect herself, because there are very few public shelters. After each air raid, the scene on the streets is unbearable to witness, as residents rushing home find their houses destroyed and their loved ones injured or killed, leading to inconsolable wailing. (Reuters, 13th)

Madrid – Rebel artillery heavily bombarded the capital today, with approximately 150 casualties. (National Dispatch, 14th)

(Havas, 13th)

Seeing this, Benavides announced the suspension of the vote count. The Congress then passed a bill recognizing Benavides' unprecedented re-election for three years. (National Dispatch, 13th)

Catalonia Autonomous Region Prepares to Fight for Independence, its mountainous terrain hard to conquer, Spanish military faces great difficulty 71

Barcelona - Catalonia is now fully prepared to engage the Nationalist army. This is not only a chapter in the revolutionary history of Catalonia, but also a genuine war for independence. It is generally believed that the Nationalist Commander-in-Chief, Franco, will conquer Madrid as his first step and then attack this semi-independent region, which includes the four northeastern provinces of Spain of Barcelona, Tarragona, Lleida and Girona. However, according to experienced senior opinions, unless Franco obtains the assistance of foreign troops, Catalonia, with its mountainous terrain, will be difficult to conquer... (Reuters, 14th) Public justice, after Hungarian nationals expressed gratitude, all await the final victory of public justice. The Hungarian Regent, Admiral Horthy, will personally go to Italy in the near future to extend sincere condolences to His Majesty the King of Italy and Emperor of Abyssinia," etc. All members of Congress cheered and paid respect to Ciano upon hearing this statement. (Havas, 13th)

Budapest, Hungary – Responsible officials here commented on the above communiqué from the Little Entente, stating that the Little Entente had previously proposed to Hungary that it be allowed to enjoy equal rights to armament, but on the condition that Hungary concludes a mutual assistance treaty with the Little Entente. The "security guarantees" mentioned in this communiqué from the Little Entente often refer to this mutual assistance treaty. On the Hungarian side, it is believed that Hungary cannot assume the obligations of mutual assistance to countries that still maintain territorial claims to this day. Therefore, the Hungarian side rejected this proposal from the Little Entente at that time. As for Hungary's request for equal rights to armament, it cannot be accompanied by any reservations whatsoever. (Havas, 14th)

(Rome) – Well-informed sources recently explained that the reason why the Foreign Ministers' Meeting of Italy, Austria, and Hungary supported Hungary's request for equal rights to armament was because Hungary has suffered unfair treatment since the European War, such as limited armament, which is just one aspect. Therefore, it is advocated that such injustices be rectified. This advocacy is not intended to be hostile to any other country. In short, once Hungary implements its rearmament, it will be done in a gradual manner, so that all neighboring countries can adjust their own armament based on Hungary's military strength. (Havas, 13th)

Proceedings of the 17th League of Nations Assembly (3) (Continued) 73

1. The question of Abyssinia's representation... 2. The process of our country being elected as a member of the Administrative Council and a judge of the Hague... 6. Conclusion...

The Sixth Committee etc. discussed various political issues, but few were related to our country, and because our representative Guo needed to liaise and contact representatives from various countries regarding the election of members of the Administrative Council and the re-election of the Hague Tribunal, Secretary Liu Kai sometimes attended the committee. When discussing the problem of international refugees, the committee, based on the proposal of the subcommittee, passed the dispatch of the Eastern Refugee Investigation Group, which our side also seconded.

3. Reorganization of the League of Nations Covenant

Question Since the Argentine government proposed the topic of reorganizing the covenant, a preliminary discussion was held at the League of Nations Assembly on July 1st this year, and a resolution was passed on the 4th, instructing the Administrative Council to notify the countries to express their opinions before the September Assembly. Now, more than 20 countries have responded in writing, and the remaining countries that have not responded in writing have all directly stated their opinions in this Assembly through their representatives. Some of them are inevitably idealistic and not allowed by the current international situation, such as New Zealand's proposal to create an international army to protect the covenant, or that member states each contribute a portion of their army to be commanded by the League of Nations. I remember that France once had this argument, which was often debated as being too idealistic. At the same time, even if it can be realized in the future, it is questionable whether the command rights belong purely to the League of Nations. Observing the current situation of the League of Nations, if this kind of ideal can be realized, the result may inevitably create a tool for the big countries to protect themselves, which is tantamount to plotting for a tiger. It will not only fail to protect the covenant, but also put the League of Nations in a more dangerous situation, and it will be easier to create a situation of manipulation. Some advocated strengthening the sanctions measures of Article 16 of the covenant, that all geographically adjacent countries conclude military mutual assistance obligations. The so-called regional mutual assistance covenant. However, whether the conclusion of this kind of covenant should be subject to the League of Nations stipulating mandatory conclusion methods, or whether the relevant countries have the right to reserve or freely conclude, has not been seen in concrete proposals. The opinions of major countries who advocate the conclusion of this kind of covenant are largely the same. However, if this kind of covenant is not subject to the League of Nations stipulating mandatory conclusion methods, whether strong countries are willing to conclude with weak countries, or whether there is a possibility of conclusion, it will inevitably cause difficult problems. Some advocated modifying the method of unanimous voting in the Administrative Council, that when peace is threatened, the sanctions measures of the covenant do not need to be implemented through "unanimous voting" of the Administrative Council, so as to prevent aggressors from evading the law by taking advantage of their one vote. Therefore, when a situation under Article 11, Section 1 of the covenant occurs, the Administrative Council can execute it after passing a two-thirds majority vote. This view is largely the same in Russia, France, and the United Kingdom. In addition, some advocate maintaining the current status of the covenant without making any changes, but advocating that the military reduction methods stipulated in the covenant should be earnestly implemented, especially focusing on strong countries should reduce their military to achieve balance. Nordic countries such as Sweden, Norway, and Denmark can be representatives of this kind of opinion. Still others advocate determining the relationship between Article 10 and Article 16 of the covenant, so as to implement the League of Nations Covenant, the Paris Convention, and various covenants against armed usurpation concluded by South American countries. This argument is from Argentina, and the United Kingdom's opinion, in addition to the points mentioned above that are the same as Russia and France, also believes that the covenant should be separated from various peace treaties, and the circumstances of Article 19 of the covenant should be modified. As for the opinions of our government, they have been delivered to the League of Nations when the Assembly opened. Domestic newspapers have already published them, so I will not repeat them here. The League of Nations Assembly has decided to hold a meeting by the General Committee to discuss it. The date of the meeting of the committee has been set for December 7th of this year. We very much hope that the representatives of all countries will show a sincere spirit of cooperation at that time, so as to bring the arguments closer and move towards rationalization and practicalization, so as not to make the reorganization fail, drawing a tiger but resembling a dog, and instead easily creating the division situation before the European War.

4. In the General Discussion of the Assembly

My representative's speech At the general discussion of the Assembly, representatives of various countries, as usual, took the stage to express their opinions in the order of registration. My representative Gu had important analyses and criticisms of the serious situation in the Far East, the remote causes and recent consequences of the dangerous situation in Europe, our government's opinions in the League of Nations Covenant reorganization movement, the world disarmament issue, and economic conditions. Because the reporter feels the importance of the situation, I feel that the opinions expressed by my representative at the League of Nations Assembly should be paid attention to by the people of the country, so I will translate the entire draft as follows.

At the 17th Assembly, in a situation that was less energetic than in previous years, I am well aware that most of you feel uneasy about the volatile situation in Europe, and your thoughts have been disturbed by the responsibility of the important issues in this kind of practical situation. Therefore, I would like to raise some different questions about the situation in my country and the Far East in general, and say a few words, because I deeply believe that today's world has a particularly close relationship, and the problems that occur in one region are bound to be repeated in other parts. From the relationship between Asia and Europe, this is especially obvious. The repercussions of the serious events in the Far East from 1904 to 1905 in Europe and the fire in Europe from 1914 to 1918 reflected in Asia can be used as two powerful illustrations in the history of an era. What is the current situation in East Asia? I would like to briefly present two facts. The first is the amazing progress in the political and economic construction of my country in the past year. Recently, the relationship between the central government and the two southwestern provinces has been peacefully resolved, and the national political unification has been completed. The greatest successes have been achieved in public health, water conservancy work, cooperative enterprises, agricultural technology and industrial improvement, electrical transportation, motor railways, air transport, etc. The report of the commissioner of the Executive Yuan's committee has detailed descriptions of this kind of progress, and the Secretary-General's report has already cited it. The technical cooperation between my country and the League of Nations will continue to achieve satisfactory results, especially the recently established method with the League of Nations, which enables our country's experts to obtain knowledge and experience on the latest technological developments in the West, and there will be further success in cooperation. In this kind of relationship, we deeply appreciate the work of Mr. Haas. In terms of my country's currency system and foreign exchange, it has also achieved remarkable results. Since the change in foreign silver prices, my country's government has suffered for two years, but the system promulgated on November 3, 1935, has been implemented throughout the country. The results produced by this new economic policy have consolidated the currency system and stabilized exchange rates, which has been the most effective encouragement for exports. The unbalanced trade has therefore been sharply reduced. British economic expert Sir Frederick Leith-Ross has said that the steps taken have been fully proven in the results obtained. In short, my country's internal construction work has made amazing progress, even under particularly difficult circumstances. According to the observations of the American Far East Economic Survey Group, "China has shown extremely important changes. Its reform atmosphere compared with ten years ago or even five years ago is enough to break the records of centuries." In addition, I would like to say a few words about other issues in the Far East. The situation there has not only not been resolved, but preparations for war are intensifying. The constant activities of troops on the border have caused many incidents, and the armed aggression is expanding day by day, forming an extremely uneasy phenomenon, which will inevitably have a dangerous eruption, which is enough to have serious repercussions in Europe.

Speaking of the current situation in Europe, we do not feel that we can reduce our worries, especially the expansion of armaments. We are now fully fledged. I think that whether it is a large country or a small country, everyone is particularly aware that if we do not continue to maintain peace, we may be eliminated by strong powers before we are prepared. At the same time, countries are also actively working to strengthen national defense and conclude numerous regional military alliances. It seems that no country feels guaranteed at the moment. Peace is still far from being solid, which is no different from the past stage. Speaking of economic issues, as mentioned in the Secretary-General's report, it seems that many countries have evidence of revival. But whether we can be sure of the arrival of revival has become a question. From the perspective of pursuing policies that satisfy national selfish desires by using deceptive economic methods, the dubious nature of the road to economic revival is very obvious. Economic nationalism has not abandoned its illusion in countries around the world. Various commercial obstacles continue to shackle trade and hinder its development. To go further, the credibility of various treaties has been fundamentally shaken in recent years, and the dignity of various international obligations has been damaged. The meaning of the allied peaceful system and security guarantees has not been implemented as usual. Although it has been implemented recently, it has not produced the desired effect because it has been implemented slowly and is not adequate to the basic purpose of law and justice. There have been too many times of succumbing to the idea of convenience. The interests of collective peace have also been lost in the end. The history of the past few years has indicated to us that the result of adopting a compromise purpose for a temporary compulsion has often made the international order more chaotic, because the more serious and uneasy the situation, the more difficult it is to implement legal handling. Four years ago, those who mourned the meaning of the entire alliance and failed in the Far East incident may also have been aware that a similar situation is bound to occur in the West today. That kind of consciousness has been truly realized. Some may ask, in this situation, how should we ease this major problem? I am afraid that I may not be able to give you a very complete answer. I want to say a few words, but because my country feels that the current instability in the West has directly affected the Far East, I sincerely hope that this instability will be resolved as soon as possible. The Chinese delegation shares the same views as other delegations and believes that the main task of resolving the current crisis lies in trusting the League of Nations and maintaining the alliance, because this agency is the only organization in the world that maintains peace, and it can also be said to be a tool for dealing with international disputes and resolving conflicts. I have repeatedly said that the failure of the League of Nations in several major incidents in the past was not an error in the improper provisions of the covenant, but an error in the policies and methods used. The main purpose of the Assembly resolution on July 4th this year is also the same.

My government has made several recommendations in its reply to the Executive Yuan's memorandum. The recommendations have been detailed in the Secretary-General's awareness and have been distributed to you. It does not seem necessary to describe its contents in detail. In short, the purpose of this recommendation is entirely to promote the League of Nations' work to eliminate war and aggression, to eliminate war and aggression before they occur, and to contain them after they have occurred. Therefore, the League of Nations should still be given the power to deal with and implement the various methods stipulated in Article 16 of the League of Nations, so that it is in accordance with the provisions of Articles 10 and 11 of the League of Nations. If it is desired to quickly stop the half of the aggressor, the League of Nations should formulate a definition of aggression in the matter, and should formulate a rapid and effective plan in advance in order to implement the various methods of Article 16 of the League of Nations. In other words, the speed of action is the main condition for effectiveness, and preparing for a rainy day is the main condition for coping with the crisis. In order to achieve this goal, my government further suggests that the Assembly should vote on the definition of aggressors in the shortest possible time, and a standing committee of experts should be attached to the Secretariat to formulate the details of the implementation of the various methods of Article 16 of the League of Nations, so as to promote its realization when the Assembly decides to implement Article 16. As for the provision in Article 16, Section 2 that each member state should dispatch troops, my government also believes that it is very important, because this is the most important attachment to other ways of preventing aggression stipulated in that article. Only if it can be implemented at the same time can it become a perfect system for preventing aggression and war. Otherwise, the so-called sanctions can never have a rapid effect. Therefore, my government believes that this provision is worthy of research, and the competent authorities of the League of Nations should conduct research and pre-determine various implementation methods so that the League of Nations has something to rely on when world peace is threatened. At the same time, regional mutual assistance covenants should be added to conform to the spirit of the League of Nations. Another recommendation of my government lies in lifting the "unanimous voting" provision stipulated in Article 11, so as to obtain a resolution in the shortest possible time, so as to avoid the disputed matters from tending to military aggression due to delay, and then war occurs. The above points are just the big ones, not the entire recommendations. My delegation still advocates supplementing the entire recommendations when concrete discussions are held in the future. The reason why I talked about these points is just to express the sincerity of my government in supporting the League of Nations, and I am willing to express a sincere cooperation to this only agency that maintains peace, so as to promote the purpose of coexistence. At the same time, my government believes that Asian member states should occupy a seat as a director in the Administrative Council, so that my country can contribute cooperation to the Administrative Council as much as possible. On this point, I am very grateful to the Administrative Council for the warm attitude it has shown towards our proposals. The Administrative Council Reorganization Committee, which was organized last September, has considered the organization of the Administrative Council. This undertaking has been unanimously passed, and the First Committee of this Assembly has also unanimously passed it.

Huang Guotai's Gang Rampages in Zhangzhou and Xiamen, Looting on Land and Water, Allegedly with Background Support from a Certain Party 74

Xiamen Dispatch: Huang Guotai, Huang He Shu, Hong Datou, Jiang Tianci, and other bandits from Longxi and Haicheng counties in Zhangzhou Prefecture, with Huang Guotai as their leader, have regrouped with over a hundred bandits, looting in various places in the southern countryside of Zhangzhou. They have issued "black lists" in more than ten villages and towns, including Shuitou, Hongcuoqian, Xiagong, Danzhou, Mazhou, Lindun, and Hongban, demanding amounts ranging from several thousand to tens of thousands of yuan. The villagers, facing economic ruin, were unable to pay. On the 7th, the Huang bandits angrily stormed into Lindun to loot. On the evening of the 8th, they attacked Hongtang, kidnapping more than thirty villagers, releasing over twenty of the poorest, and binding the eleven they considered wealthy. They also shot and killed three people on the spot. That night, they attacked Xiayangshe, burning down two houses. On the 9th, they attacked Tianbian, killing two villagers. They are now gathered in Dongdai. The "black lists" they issue are signed by Huang Houjian (another name for Guotai), the Commander of the Fujian Independent Brigade of the Chinese People's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Army. The garrison is dispatching troops to encircle and suppress them. According to reports, Huang Guotai was a former subordinate of Wu Ci. After Wu's involvement in the Fujian Incident, he once raised the false banner of the "South China State" in Hua'an. Later, he surrendered and was incorporated into the government forces. Last winter, Wu was assassinated, and Huang became a bandit again, gathering Huang Hedong, Hong Datou, Jiang Tianci, Zheng Beizai, and others, becoming their leader. Zheng was killed by government troops this past September, and Huang took over his followers. Although each group has only twenty or thirty people, totaling just over a hundred, the depth of their harm to the people surpasses all other major bandit gangs in Zhangzhou. Their accomplices are spread throughout Longxi, Haicheng, and the cities of Zhangzhou, Shima, Damen, and Gulangyu. On land, they issue "black lists" in various villages of Longxi and Haicheng counties; on water, they collect flag fees. The so-called "black lists" are written notices demanding the payment of certain amounts of money by a deadline, threatening murder or kidnapping for non-compliance. "Flag fees" are collected from all Zhangzhou-owned ships, whether cargo or fishing boats, on the sea and rivers of Zhangzhou, requiring a monthly payment in exchange for a small flag, which serves as a guarantee of safe passage. Otherwise, they face murder and ship robbery if they encounter bandits on the way. Countless people on land and water have died because of this. Due to their widespread accomplices and extensive connections, they can rampage in the areas of Xicheng Zhangma in Zhangzhou with a small force. Repeated military suppression has failed to capture them, and local militia are also unable to curb their activities. What distinguishes them from other bandit gangs is their collusion with a certain party and their alleged background support. On the 10th of this month, the Second Brigade of the Damen Marine Police, while in Douzaiwei Coast of Beishi, Xiamen, captured Chen Jintang, a bandit who collected "flag fees" from boat owners. They found oil-printed notification slips for collecting fees, which stated, "Our headquarters is reorganizing the sea surface this time, entirely for protection purposes. We appreciate the generous assistance of all boat owners. In the future, when our headquarters achieves its goals, all favors will be repaid. The monthly fees must be paid in full between the 1st and 5th of each month. Violators will be severely punished." The slip was signed by Huang Xiongjian (of the Headquarters), Chief Manager Kang Jianying, and Deputy Manager Gan Jianwu. According to Chen's confession, "The Damen office is located behind the Wantong Opium Den on Jukou Street. The leaders are Kang and Gan. Each ship pays a 'stove fee' of ten yuan and a monthly fee of three yuan. The office has been established for over two months, and Damen can collect over three thousand yuan each month. The boat owners come to pay voluntarily. Those who do not pay are urged. The fee is split between Wantong and us. There is a door in the back of Wantong that leads to the Butterfly Dance Hall," etc. According to reports, the Wantong Opium Den, known as "Wantong Foreign Firm," is operated by Taiwanese people of Japanese nationality, and the Butterfly Dance Hall is also operated by Taiwanese people. Based on the confession, the marine police, together with the Public Security Bureau and officials from the Japanese Consulate, went to Wantong on Jukou Street to arrest them. Upon arrival, Kang, Gan, and their subordinates were already aware and immediately broke down the door and fled, firing shots along the way. The police failed to capture them and returned without conducting a search of the office. At that time, one bandit fled into a nearby house, leaving behind his hat and clothes, and escaped by climbing over the roof. Afterward, the homeowner took the clothes to the Third Branch of the Public Security Bureau. At night, someone actually went to the Jukou Street area to inquire, saying that someone had left clothes at a certain house in the afternoon and they had come to retrieve them, but they could not remember which house or the address. None of the nearby residents dared to tell them where it was. After inquiring for a long time without success, they left. They were extremely bold. Huang Guotai joined Weng Cixing's pseudo-Datong League and the Heng Society organized by Weng this summer. After Weng surrendered, Huang remained a bandit. Therefore, he still uses the banner of the so-called "Anti-Japanese National Salvation Army" and imitates the organization of the Heng Society to form a secret society, forcing people on land and water to join and using the character "sword" as a symbol. All those who join his gang must have the character "sword" in their names, such as Huang, who changed his name to "Houjian," and Kang Jianying and Gan Jianwu. The "flag" given to ships at sea as protection is a small yellow flag with a sword drawn on it. The more than three thousand yuan in flag fees collected by the Damen office is used to support the bandits' families in Xiamen and Gulangyu and to purchase guns and ammunition. Kang and Gan are the chief and deputy directors of his Damen branch. Damen, Beishi, Douzaiwei, Nanshi, Xiagang, and the anchorages for sailing ships in Gulangyu are all within his sphere of influence. Those who are late in paying "flag fees" are hung up and beaten. One old boatman was forced to pay fifty-seven yuan for ten months of flag fees and "stove fees" at once, having already paid thirty yuan in installments and still owing twenty-seven yuan. In addition, Haimen, Baishuiying, Shima, and Zhangzhou all have branch offices, while the pseudo-headquarters is located in Chendi, under the jurisdiction of Haicheng. Huang Guotai himself is mostly in Chendi, but also often comes to Damen, accompanied by several people carrying Mauser pistols as guards. It is obvious that he has background support from a certain party and that he can rampage in Xicheng Zhangma without defeat shows the breadth of his connections and the depth of his control over the general population. (November 13th)

Wuxi: Resolution of the Private Soil in Postal Packages Case 78

Gu Fuqi, a clerk in the parcel section of the local Postal Administration, committed suicide by electrocution at home on the morning of August 26th of this year. Beforehand, he wrote a suicide note and left it to the administrative officer. After the incident, the suicide note was seized by the county government. Because its contents involved the issue of private soil carried in postal packages, Xu Fuchang and postal workers Yang Dahui, Tong Jiayao, postal carriers Tian Changhai, Yu Afu, Yu Shousheng, Wu Jide, Cheng Xiangfu, Zhang Lianyuan, and others were all summoned to the county and escorted to the Second District Security Command for interrogation and detention. Three months have passed. The military court has now determined that Xu Fuchang and the other ten people are not related to this case and ordered their release on bail. Due to procedural delays, they must be released on bail on Monday. As for the reinstatement of postal workers Yang Dahui and postal carriers Tian Changhai and the other eight people, the matter must await the bureau chief's request to the Postal Administration for further review.

The 12th was the anniversary of the general manager's birthday. The branch office clerks came to the city beforehand to participate in a Qixia Mountain tour. Unexpectedly, thieves broke into the office in the middle of the night on that day, pried open the bank's safe, and stole three thousand six hundred yuan in cash and silver dollars stored inside out of the eight thousand yuan inside the safe. It was not until dawn that it was discovered that the front and back doors of the room were not open, only the back door of Mujin was found to be wide open, with a bamboo pole leaning against the wall, suggesting it was used to climb over the wall. The incident was immediately reported to the Sixth Branch of the Public Security Bureau for investigation. It was quickly determined that the night watchman, Lao Si, was highly suspicious and was taken to the police station for questioning.

Fuzhou: Director of the Children's Home Tours Eastern Fujian 82

Since taking office, Tong Hangshi, President of the Fujian Provincial High Court, has spared no effort in rectifying the judiciary. Last year, he went to Southern and Northern Fujian to conduct inspections in person, improving all matters that needed improvement or reform based on the actual situation. Therefore, the people of Fujian have given him the reputation of "Iron-Faced Tong." The 18th of this month is his sixtieth birthday, and relatives and friends have launched an initiative to celebrate his birthday. However, Director Tong, citing the ongoing national crisis, declined, but old friends in Fujian, because Director Tong is known for his integrity, had Zhang Qin, a former compiler of the Hanlin Academy, write an article to celebrate his birthday. Director Tong, feeling unable to refuse, decided to leave the provincial capital to avoid the celebrations and inspect the judiciary in Eastern Fujian. The judiciary in Fujian was previously extremely dark, with deeply entrenched problems. After inspections and reforms in Southern and Northern Fujian, the situation has been renewed. The situation in Eastern Fujian is different. In order to conduct on-site investigations into the advantages and disadvantages, he is taking this opportunity to tour the area to facilitate the rectification.

Shangrao: Commissioner Xiao Improves District Administration 83

Xiao Bingzhang, the newly appointed Supervisory Commissioner of the Sixth Administrative District of Jiangxi, has followed Premier Sun in revolution for many years. He was recently appointed by the authorities to preside over the district's administration. His administrative policy is to start with the development of the economy. According to Hu Weiwen, a senior official of the commissioner's office, the district's situation and administrative policies are as follows: (1) Providing loans to rural areas. The district is rich in products, such as Guangfeng County's tobacco, which was sold overseas in large quantities in the past. However, due to local turmoil, production has sharply declined. Other products, such as Hekou's paper and Yiyang's rice, are in the same situation. It is now planned to negotiate with the banking sector to provide loans for relief in order to increase and improve products. (2) Promoting cooperation. The products of each county are sold by merchants, resulting in heavy exploitation. Producers are the first to suffer, and merchants lack organization, leading to high transportation costs and losses. Now that the Zhegan Railway runs through the territory, it is planned to form large-scale transportation and sales cooperatives to facilitate sales. (3) Adjusting consumption. The district's customs are mostly simple, but unnecessary consumption is unavoidable. It is now planned to implement a thrifty movement in accordance with the principles of national economic construction, guiding consumption into the right track. Other major tasks, such as managing warehousing, promoting education, and training strong men, should also be implemented in accordance with government orders.

Local News

Local Business Community Prepares to Welcome the Nanyang Commercial Inspection Group 84

The Nanyang Commercial Inspection Group departed the country on July 16th, traveling through Manila, Surabaya, Semarang, Batavia, Singapore, Kuala Lumpur, Ipoh, Siam, Penang, Medan, and other places. They were warmly welcomed by overseas Chinese. In each location, they held exhibitions of domestic products, attracting crowds of men and women. Various foreign governments provided preferential treatment, treating them as foreign guests. The group negotiated with economic authorities in various countries and engaged in national diplomacy, receiving much praise from overseas Chinese. The group also gave public speeches in various locations, publicizing the current situation in China and the government's concern for overseas Chinese, which greatly enhanced the patriotic sentiments of overseas Chinese. As a result, there are already three or four groups that want to organize homeland inspection groups. The group has now returned to China on the French postal ship General Xiafei. The following is a summary of the situation:

Philippines: Upon the group's arrival in Manila, the capital of the Philippines, with the assistance of the Chinese General Chamber of Commerce, under the leadership of Chairman Li Qingquan, they held an exhibition of domestic products. Philippine President Quezon and Vice President Osmeña were very supportive. At the same time, the group negotiated with the China-Philippines National Association, striving to enhance the friendship between China and the Philippines. Therefore, the exhibition was as grand as a carnival. The Philippine market is almost entirely dominated by Japanese goods. Although American goods can be imported duty-free, they still cannot compete. The shipment of domestic goods to the Philippines has been decreasing year by year. The group has now reached a strong agreement with major Chinese importers in the area, under the principle of mutual assistance, to vigorously seek to expand the domestic goods market in the Philippines. The group will be able to realize this after returning to China.

Dutch East Indies: Including Surabaya, Semarang, Batavia, and Medan, four major ports. Except for Semarang, which was not included in the exhibition program due to special reasons, grand exhibitions of domestic products were held in the other three ports. After the group entered the country, they were formally received by the Dutch East Indies Ministry of Economy, so all proceedings were very convenient. However, due to import restrictions, the import of domestic goods faced extreme difficulties. Overseas Chinese in Java, Sumatra, and other places mainly operate as wholesalers, while importers are mostly in the hands of Europeans. Group leader Gao Shiheng negotiated with the Ministry of Economy, and the Dutch East Indies government issued a special import permit to show accommodation. However, the final promotion method still needs further effort.

British Malaya: In addition to holding a domestic exhibition in Singapore and Penang, the group visited Kuala Lumpur, Ipoh, and other places, and was greatly welcomed by overseas Chinese groups. Overseas Chinese celebrities such as Hu Wenhu, Chen Jiageng, and Liang Shannan all provided warm hospitality. Overseas Chinese in Malaya have a higher level of education compared to other parts of Nanyang and have a better understanding of domestic goods. Therefore, the domestic exhibition held at the Great World in Singapore every year has achieved good results. The group held the exhibition at the Daguan Garden Amusement Park in Penang. The admission ticket for the amusement park cost two jiao, but there were 6,000 visitors every day, which shows its popularity. The organizations of overseas Chinese groups in Kuala Lumpur, Ipoh, and other places are exceptionally sound. The addresses of the Chinese Chambers of Commerce are all tall and magnificent. Since 1935, the prices of rubber and tin in Malaya have increased, resulting in a significant recovery. If domestic goods are cheap and suitable, there is great hope.

Siam: Siam has 2.5 million overseas Chinese, and Chinese shops are everywhere. Currently, many senior officials in the Siamese government are of Chinese descent. After the group arrived in Siam, the welcome was no less grand than that of the previous Siamese inspection group. Siam is an agricultural country, so all industrial products rely on imports. In the past, Chinese people had very little understanding of the Siamese market. The group's inspection found that there was great hope and that there were many goods that could be shipped for sale but had not yet been sent to the market. Therefore, the number of people visiting the domestic exhibition every day was extremely crowded. During his stay in Siam, Group Leader Gao gathered various leaders to discuss the results. As a first step, they organized a domestic goods company. At that time, they raised a capital of 70,000 yuan and planned to realize it in the shortest possible time, so the future is very optimistic. The group has completed its work in Medan and departed from Medan on November 3 to return to China, making slight stops in Singapore, Saigon, and other places, and returning on the original ship (French postal ship General Xiafei). The local business community has prepared a warm welcome to the group, which has traveled thousands of miles to promote domestic goods, and there will be a grand occasion at that time.

Purpose of the Trip: Sun replied to the reporter's question, saying that he had three missions for this trip to Shanghai: (1) To pay respects on behalf of Chairman Song and assist with the funeral arrangements, to liaise with the funeral committee, and to decide whether to build a cemetery in advance in accordance with Mr. Duan's wishes to be buried in the Western Hills of Beiping at a state funeral, or to wait until the coffin is moved to Beiping before determining the location, so that Beiping can make all the arrangements in advance. Chairman Song, because of Mr. Wu's efforts in national affairs during his lifetime and his desolate circumstances after his death, specially donated 2,000 yuan as a contribution, which was brought by me to Mr. Wu's family. Smuggling Issues: The issue of smuggling in North China is complex and difficult to resolve. Previously, Minister Kong sent Counselor Li (Qingxuan) to North Hebei and Chahar, and Secretary-General Ge (Dingyuan) of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council came south. The discussions were only on how to clear smuggled goods, and there was no way to stop the source. Therefore, the clearing of smuggled goods has not been able to proceed immediately. As for how many smuggled goods there are, it is difficult to count because they come and go at any time.

Security in Hebei and Chahar: As for the situation in North China, the security in Hebei and Chahar is very solid. The situation in Suiyuan is not as serious as the rumors suggest. Chairman Song's talk the other day can give a general overview. Reports say that there are 30,000 to 40,000 pseudo-bandit troops, which is an exaggeration. In reality, there are only over 10,000 people. They are being exploited and used by others to cause some disturbances as a way to repay them.

All were approved for publication and listed for announcement. Wang Zhengting Talks About Sino-American Relations: China Welcomes Foreign Investment, Only Requires No Damage to Chinese Sovereignty 93

According to the Shenzhou News Agency, Wang Zhengting, the newly appointed ambassador to the United States, will depart for his post in the middle of next month. Yesterday, Wang met with foreign reporters at his residence to discuss Sino-American relations. Wang said that the friendship between China and the United States has existed for more than 200 years, and the relationship has always been extremely harmonious. He hopes that Sino-American relations can continue to improve in the future. Under the principle of not harming Chinese sovereignty, the United States can help China develop its resources as much as possible. China's current lack of capital is similar to the situation in the United States 150 years ago. Later, with the help of European countries, especially the United Kingdom, the United States developed its abundant resources and became prosperous. Therefore, during the European war, the United States was able to help the United Kingdom's recovery with its surplus. This situation has many lessons for China. China's capital supply is naturally limited during this period of national crisis, but the development of natural resources is unlimited. Therefore, China now welcomes unlimited investment of foreign capital. China is an ancient country with a long history, but its industry is still in its infancy. If it receives assistance from friendly countries, the prospect of China's development is very promising. The reporter then asked about the issue of the United States abolishing consular jurisdiction in China. Wang said that this is still a pending case. China not only has this hope for the United States, but will also use appropriate methods in the same spirit to seek the same solution from all countries. Wang finally said that the situation in the Far East is indeed in a dangerous state, but it is not as severe as in 1913 or 1932. He hopes that this serious situation can be resolved as soon as possible. It is also learned that Mr. Wang plans to meet with former U.S. Secretary of State Stimson next month after arriving in the United States.

Government Agencies Use Domestic Products: Five Supplementary Suggestions Sent by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and Municipal Local Association to the Executive Yuan and Relevant Ministries Requesting Adoption 96

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Shanghai Municipal Local Association believe that the seven articles of the "Provisional Measures for Government Agencies to Purchase Domestic Products" passed by the Executive Yuan this time are a profound encouragement to domestic industry. Based on their considerations, they listed five suggestions and sent them to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Industry, requesting adoption. The original text is recorded as follows: "To the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Industry in Nanjing: The seven articles of the 'Provisional Measures for Government Agencies to Purchase Domestic Products' passed by the Executive Yuan, reflect the central government's determination to promote domestic products, which has advanced from encouragement and advocacy to active promotion. The encouragement to domestic industry is profound and far-reaching. The article stating that any government agency that does not use domestic products when available will be considered an uneconomical expenditure and will not be approved for reimbursement is particularly encouraging and should be heeded throughout the country. After unanimously endorsing this, our association wishes to extend it to all industrial and commercial organizations nationwide for uniform implementation, in order to promote it universally. However, considering what concerns us, we respectfully submit our humble opinions: (1) Creating a catalog of domestic products and distributing it to various agencies for selection is an excellent method. However, before creating the catalog, it seems that specialists should be appointed to conduct a thorough review to ensure appropriateness. (2) Before approving the registration and issuing a certificate of domestic origin to domestic factories that have not been registered, in order to prevent non-domestic products from being falsely represented, it is necessary to consult widely and thoroughly to confirm that they are truly domestic products before issuing the certificate and creating the catalog, prioritizing quality over quantity. (3) For merchants who sell non-domestic products as domestic products, there are already measures in place for punishment. The fundamental solution is to hope that the unified domestic products company planned by the Executive Yuan will be realized as soon as possible, so that domestic products companies can be established in various regions in order for government agencies to purchase them. (4) For necessary items that are essential for daily life and have a significant impact on the national economy, it is hoped that the Executive Yuan and relevant ministries will work with the industrial sector to find ways to provide assistance and prepare for self-production. (5) Due to the full support and promotion of the Executive Yuan and relevant ministries, all products of domestic factories will inevitably have smooth sales. In the event that this leads to price increases, which would affect purchasers, it would betray the original intention of the Executive Yuan and relevant ministries. We request that a notice be issued in advance to warn against this in order to facilitate implementation. The above five points are merely humble opinions, and we trust that the Executive Yuan and relevant ministries will carefully consider them. We deeply admire and are eager to see the benefits. We respectfully submit this appeal and hope for your consideration. Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce and Shanghai Municipal Local Association, respectfully, sealed."

China International Famine Relief Commission Receives Letters and Telegrams From Sichuan Requesting Disaster Relief 98

The China International Famine Relief Commission at 97 Renji Road has repeatedly received reports from Sichuan that the drought is extremely severe. Details are as follows: The Hechuan County Government of Sichuan Province stated in a letter: "This year, our county has been hit by a series of disasters, including wind, hail, and earthquakes, which have devastated agricultural production. Since the beginning of summer, the river god has wreaked havoc, causing significant losses to residents along the river in three or four incidents. Most severely, the drought has been devastating. Since summer, the rice and sorghum have mostly withered and died, and even the potato has no chance of survival. As winter approaches, the fields are all red. It is difficult for villagers to find water to drink, and there is no way to plant the winter grain. There is no harvest in either paddy fields or dry fields. Distressed people gather and rob grain, creating dangerous situations. The future is long and unimaginable. We earnestly request generous assistance to help the disaster victims." The Liangshan County Government stated in a letter: "Between spring and summer this year, our county had timely rain and sunshine, and the fields were all sown. However, since mid-summer, the scorching sun has been raging, and it has not rained for a long time. The seedlings have all withered, and there is no hope for beans and sorghum. Farmers in various villages, supporting the old and carrying the young, carrying withered rice and sorghum, are calling for help along the way, displaced and scattered, which is a tragic sight. We request allocation of funds for relief. Your kindness will be deeply appreciated." The Relief Branch of Qu County stated in a letter: "Our county has been unfortunate in recent years, with disasters occurring repeatedly. This summer, there was another severe drought, and as far as the eye can see, the land is red and there is no harvest. The bark and roots of trees have been dug up almost entirely, and even parents and wives cannot protect each other. Abandonment and displacement are everywhere, and the situation is tragic and unbearable. What crime have the people of Qu County committed to suffer such a calamity? Merciful heavens, when will it end? We ask your commission to advocate and raise funds to save these disaster victims. Your merit will be immeasurable."

Expanded Anti-Drug Campaign: Municipal Police Bureau Works Intensively 100

Since the expansion of the anti-drug campaign began in this city on the 10th of this month, the Municipal Police Bureau immediately ordered all officers and police in each branch to organize propaganda teams and conduct propaganda in various districts. All investigators of the bureau were also ordered to go out to supervise the propaganda, paying special attention to factories and shantytowns, and persuading drug addicts to voluntarily quit as soon as possible. At the same time, the bureau is currently exchanging third-term limited-period opium smoking licenses. Many smokers are hesitant to exchange their licenses, and the deadline for exchanging licenses is the 30th of this month. The time is very short. Therefore, the bureau is taking advantage of this propaganda period to simultaneously conduct door-to-door inspections and persuade smokers to exchange their licenses. In recent days, the bureau's work has been very intense. Dai Lizhen, the head of the anti-drug department, went to the Xinzha Road Branch, Hengfeng Road, Mongolia Road, Pusong, and Xujiahui police stations in the previous two days to convene all working police officers to give instructions, encouraging them to redouble their efforts in order to achieve the greatest effect. Recently, due to the enthusiastic participation of drug addicts in quitting, the number of beds is insufficient. Yesterday morning (the 14th), Dai also went to the Shanghai North Drug Rehabilitation Hospital to discuss with the hospital director, Mei Zhuosheng, about finding ways to increase the number of beds to meet the demand. Dai also pointed out that in recent investigations, the number of repeat offenders who relapsed after quitting drugs was very large. He then convened the drug addicts in the hospital and gave a speech urging them to completely repent after quitting and not relapse again, so as not to be caught in the criminal net. The listeners were all moved.
